<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">2015 Pacific hurricane season</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<tr>
<td class="hlist noprint nowrap" colspan="2" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;"><a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane seasons</a><br/>
<a href="/wiki/2013_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2013 Pacific hurricane season">2013</a>, <a href="/wiki/2014_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2014 Pacific hurricane season">2014</a>, <b>2015</b>, <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">2016</a>, <a href="/wiki/2017_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2017 Pacific hurricane season">2017</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The <b>2015 Pacific hurricane season</b> is the second-most active <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Pacific hurricane season">Pacific hurricane season</a> on record, with 26 named storms, only behind the <a href="/wiki/1992_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1992 Pacific hurricane season">1992 season</a>. A record-tying 16 of the storms became hurricanes, and a record 11 storms became major hurricanes throughout the season. The central Pacific, the portion of the eastern Pacific between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">International Dateline</a> and <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140°W</a>, had its most active year on record, with fifteen tropical cyclones forming in or entering the basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Moreover, the season was the second most active season in terms of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a>, with a total of 286 ACE units. The season officially started on May 15 in the East Pacific Ocean and on June 1 in the Central Pacific; they both ended on November 30. These dates conventionally delimit the period of each year when most tropical cyclones form in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific basin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-season_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-season-2">[2]</a></sup> However, the formation of tropical cyclones is possible at any time of the year. This was shown when a tropical depression existed on December 31. The above-average activity during the season was attributed in part to the strong <a href="/wiki/2014%E2%80%9316_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014–16 El Niño event">2014–16 El Niño event</a>.</p>
<p>The season featured several long-tracking and powerful storms, although land impact was often minimal. In June, Hurricane Blanca, an early season Category 4 hurricane, killed four people due to rough seas. Hurricane Carlos caused minor damage while passing a short distance off the coast of Mexico. On August 29, three Category 4 hurricanes (Kilo, Ignacio, Jimena) were all active simultaneously for the first time in recorded history. Moisture from <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Linda_(2015)" title="Hurricane Linda (2015)">Hurricane Linda</a> contributed to storms that killed 21 people in <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">Utah</a>. Later in September, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marty_(2015)" title="Hurricane Marty (2015)">Hurricane Marty</a> was responsible for $30 million (2015 USD) in damages to the southwestern Mexican coast. In October, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a> became the most intense hurricane ever recorded in the Western Hemisphere, with a central pressure of 872 mbar (hPa; 25.75 inHg) and 1-minute <a href="/wiki/Maximum_sustained_wind" title="Maximum sustained wind">sustained winds</a> of 215 mph (345 km/h). After also becoming the strongest landfalling <a href="/wiki/Pacific_hurricane" title="Pacific hurricane">Pacific hurricane</a> on record, Patricia claimed 13 lives and was responsible for $460 million in damages. The season's activity continued into November, when <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandra_(2015)" title="Hurricane Sandra (2015)">Hurricane Sandra</a> became the strongest hurricane ever recorded in that month.</p>
<p></p>

<p>On April 10, 2015, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Servicio_Meteorol%C3%B3gico_Nacional" title="Servicio Meteorológico Nacional">Servicio Meteorológico Nacional</a> (SMN) issued its first outlook for the Pacific hurricane season, forecasting 19 named storms, 11 hurricanes, and 4 major hurricanes. The organization listed a set of seasons with similar atmospheric and oceanic conditions, including <a href="/wiki/1982_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1982 Pacific hurricane season">1982</a>, <a href="/wiki/1986_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1986 Pacific hurricane season">1986</a>, <a href="/wiki/1991_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1991 Pacific hurricane season">1991</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1994 Pacific hurricane season">1994</a>, <a href="/wiki/2002_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2002 Pacific hurricane season">2002</a>, and <a href="/wiki/2014_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2014 Pacific hurricane season">2014</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-0410SMN_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-0410SMN-5">[5]</a></sup> On May 27, the <a href="/wiki/National_Oceanic_and_Atmospheric_Administration" title="National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration">National Oceanic and Atmospheric Administration</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Climate_Prediction_Center" title="Climate Prediction Center">Climate Prediction Center</a> (CPC) released its forecast for the year, highlighting a 70% chance of an above-average season with 15–22 named storms, 7–12 hurricanes, 5–8 major hurricanes, and an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) index range of 110–190% of the median. While both organizations cited an intensifying <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2014-16_El_Ni%C3%B1o_event" title="2014-16 El Niño event">El Niño</a> as a cause of increased activity, the CPC also highlighted the difference in global sea surface temperature patterns in 2015 versus the 1995–2014 period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-0410SMN_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-0410SMN-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-0527NOAA_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-0527NOAA-6">[6]</a></sup> The season ended up exceeding all of these forecasts with 26 named storms, 16 hurricanes, 11 major hurricanes, and an ACE index at more than 200% of the median.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Seasonal_summary">Seasonal summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Seasonal summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_the_2015_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="Timeline of the 2015 Pacific hurricane season">Timeline of the 2015 Pacific hurricane season</a></div>
<center>
<div class="timeline-wrapper"><map id="timeline_682b5f199d59956ba7b5e93f0a1cf7db" name="timeline_682b5f199d59956ba7b5e93f0a1cf7db">

<area alt="Hurricane Patricia" coords="493,111,601,132" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Patricia"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Marty (2015)" coords="430,39,521,59" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marty_(2015)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Marty (2015)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Linda (2015)" coords="375,126,466,147" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Linda_(2015)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Linda (2015)"/>
<area alt="Typhoon Halola" coords="207,68,304,89" href="/wiki/Typhoon_Halola" shape="rect" title="Typhoon Halola"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Carlos (2015)" coords="138,39,235,59" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carlos_(2015)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Carlos (2015)"/>
<area alt="Hurricane Blanca (2015)" coords="116,24,213,45" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Blanca_(2015)" shape="rect" title="Hurricane Blanca (2015)"/>
<area alt="Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale" coords="602,220,843,240" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" shape="rect" title="Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale"/></map><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/timeline/682b5f199d59956ba7b5e93f0a1cf7db.png" usemap="#timeline_682b5f199d59956ba7b5e93f0a1cf7db"/></div>
</center>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kilo,_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5000" data-file-width="9000" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kilo%2C_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg/350px-Kilo%2C_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kilo%2C_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg/525px-Kilo%2C_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Kilo%2C_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg/700px-Kilo%2C_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg 2x" width="350"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Kilo,_Ignacio_and_Jimena_2015-08-30_0930Z.jpg" title="Aumentar"></a></div>
Hurricanes Kilo <i>(left)</i>, Ignacio <i>(center)</i>, and Jimena <i>(right)</i>, all at major hurricane intensity, spanning the Central and Eastern Pacific basins on August 30</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Accumulated_Cyclone_Energy" title="Accumulated Cyclone Energy">Accumulated Cyclone Energy</a> (ACE) index for the season was 160.4825 units in the East Pacific and 126.03 units in the Central Pacific. The total ACE for the Northeast Pacific basin in 2015 amounted to 286.5125 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[nb 1]</a></sup></p>
<p>The season's first named storm, Andres, developed two weeks after the official start of the season. Andres later reached peak intensity as a Category 4 hurricane on June 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndresD17_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-AndresD17-8">[7]</a></sup> On June 3, Blanca became both earliest second hurricane and second major hurricane in the basin since reliable records began.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlancaD9_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-BlancaD9-9">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlancaD12_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-BlancaD12-10">[9]</a></sup> This broke the previous record by seven days set by <a href="/wiki/2014_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Cristina" title="2014 Pacific hurricane season">Hurricane Cristina</a> the previous year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup> On June 13, Hurricane Carlos became the second earliest third hurricane on record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">After an inactive period for about a month, activity resumed in mid-July with five systems forming in short succession (three in the central Pacific and two in the east Pacific). One of these systems, Tropical Storm Ela, became the third earliest forming Central Pacific storm on record at the time. Tropical Storm Halola crossed the International Date Line two days later. Next month, hurricanes Guillermo and Hilda both affected Hawaii, while Hurricane Loke became the record breaking fifth named storm in the Central Pacific. Soon after Loke dissipated, Tropical Storm Kilo (which formed before Loke) strengthened into a hurricane while Ignacio and Jimena were being named. Late on August 29th, all three storms exploded into Category 4 major hurricanes.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> These three major hurricanes were all active on August 29, being the first time in the historical record that three or more major hurricanes existed simultaneously in the Pacific, east of the International Date Line (180ºW).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter.com_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iweathernet.com_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-iweathernet.com-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Tropical Storm Kevin formed, but was short-lived, and Kevin and Ignacio dissipated on September 5. Hurricane Linda formed on September 6 and peaked as a Category 3 major hurricane, yet dissipated four days later. After Jimena and Linda dissipated on September 10, a short 9 day pause of tropical activity occurred, the first since June. Then, on September 19, Malia developed, with Sixteen-E developing the day after. Sixteen-E quickly moved over <a href="/wiki/Baja_California" title="Baja California">Baja California</a> and mainland <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> before dissipating on September 21. Malia dissipated on September 22, but was followed three days later by Tropical Depression Six-C, which intensified into Tropical Storm Niala southeast of Hawaii, prompting a tropical storm watch for <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_County,_Hawaii" title="Hawaii County, Hawaii">Hawaii County</a>, the "big island" or "<a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawai'i</a>". Marty developed, became a hurricane just off Mexico, yet dissipated out to sea.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> With the formation of Oho on October 3, the 2015 season surpassed <a href="/wiki/1992_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1992 Pacific hurricane season">1992</a> and <a href="/wiki/1994_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1994 Pacific hurricane season">1994</a> as the most active year on record in the Central Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7Cdisc1_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-7Cdisc1-15">[14]</a></sup> On October 18 Olaf strengthened to a hurricane at 9.4°N making it the southernmost-forming hurricane in the east Pacific basin. Then it strengthened to a major hurricane at 9.9°N, making it the southernmost-forming major hurricane in the basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup> In comparison, the southernmost-forming tropical cyclone in the basin is <a href="/wiki/1983_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Adolph" title="1983 Pacific hurricane season">Adolph</a> of <a href="/wiki/1983_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1983 Pacific hurricane season">1983</a> which became a tropical depression at 7.1°N.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TC_Report_-_Polo_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-TC_Report_-_Polo-17">[16]</a></sup></p>
