<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">When <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Patricia</a> rapidly intensified into a Category 4 hurricane on October 22, the season became only the second – after 1992 – in the East Pacific satellite era to see the formation of a record ten major hurricanes. Not only did Patricia tie the record for the 2015 East Pacific hurricane season with 1992,</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> it became the strongest hurricane in the basin with a pressure of 892 millibars, breaking the previous record of 902 millibars, set by <a href="/wiki/1997_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1997 Pacific hurricane season">1997</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Linda_(1997)" title="Hurricane Linda (1997)">Hurricane Linda</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> Patricia subsequently became the strongest tropical cyclone on record in the Western Hemisphere in terms of barometric pressure. It had a central pressure of 872 millibars, the lowest ever observed by the National Hurricane Center which has jurisdiction in the East Pacific and Atlantic, and the second-lowest pressure globally, behind <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Tip" title="Typhoon Tip">Typhoon Tip</a> of 1979 which had a central pressure of 870 millibars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[18]</a></sup> Additionally, its maximum sustained winds of 215 mph (345 km/h) were the strongest ever reliably recorded or estimated anywhere globally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PatriciaTCR_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-PatriciaTCR-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">After Olaf dissipated on October 27, there was no further tropical activity until Tropical Storm Rick formed in mid-November. With the formation of Tropical Storm Sandra, two named storms developed within the month of November, which tied the record with <a href="/wiki/2006_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2006 Pacific hurricane season">2006</a> for being the most active November since Pacific hurricane records began.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Two days later, Sandra strengthened into a major hurricane, bringing the season total to a record eleven. Its peak winds of 150 mph (240 km/h) surpassed <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Kenneth" title="2011 Pacific hurricane season">Hurricane Kenneth</a> of 2011 for the strongest November Pacific hurricane in terms of sustained winds, while its minimum central pressure of 934 millibars also surpassed Kenneth for the most intense November Pacific hurricane in terms of central pressure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SandraTCR_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-SandraTCR-21">[20]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Sandra's dissipation marked the last tropical storm to exist inside of the hurricane season. Despite this, over a month later, favorable conditions inside the Central Pacific lead to the formation of Tropical Depression Nine-C on December 31. The depression never reached tropical storm strength, leaving the season one named storm shy of tying the <a href="/wiki/1992_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1992 Pacific hurricane season">1992 season's</a> record of 27 named storms. It dissipated that same day, marking the latest ending to a Pacific hurricane season on record.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Systems">Systems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Systems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Andres">Hurricane Andres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Hurricane Andres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg"><img alt="Andres 2015-05-31 1825Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg/150px-Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg/225px-Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg/300px-Andres_2015-05-31_1825Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Andres_2015_track.png"><img alt="Andres 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Andres_2015_track.png/150px-Andres_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Andres_2015_track.png/225px-Andres_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Andres_2015_track.png/300px-Andres_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 28 – June 4</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  937 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On May 23, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hurricane_Center" title="National Hurricane Center">National Hurricane Center</a> began monitoring the potential for tropical cyclogenesis well south of Mexico over the following days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup> A large area of disturbed weather formed two days later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> steadily organizing to become Tropical Depression One-E at 09:00 UTC on May 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> With an increase in <a href="/wiki/Rainband" title="Rainband">spiral banding</a> and an expanding <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a>, the depression was upgraded to Tropical Storm Andres six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> Directed west-northwest and eventually northwest by a <a href="/wiki/Ridge_(meteorology)" title="Ridge (meteorology)">ridge</a> over Mexico, the cyclone steadily organized despite moderate northerly shear. At 21:00 UTC on May 29, Andres intensified into a Category 1 hurricane,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> and by 15:00 UTC on May 30, the cyclone further strengthened into a Category 2 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> Although forecasts did not indicate additional strengthening, Andres began a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a> the following day, becoming one of only five major hurricanes during the month of May at 21:00 UTC and further intensifying into a Category 4 at 03:00 UTC on June 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Andres ultimately reached its peak intensity early on June 1 with winds of 145 mph (230 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AndresTCR_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-AndresTCR-30">[29]</a></sup> Thereafter, the system moved over cooler waters and into a more stable environment which imparted weakening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> Over the next few days, Andres continued to weaken, and by June 3, the NHC determined that it had weakened into a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup> Further weakening ensured, with Andres being designated as a remnant low on June 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup></p>
<p>Moisture extending from the remnants of Andres brought light rain to parts of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southwest_United_States" title="Southwest United States">Southwest United States</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a> having measurable precipitation on June 5 for the first time since records began in 1896.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup> This moisture further extended into <a href="/wiki/Colorado" title="Colorado">Colorado</a>, resulting in scattered severe thunderstorms.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Blanca">Hurricane Blanca</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hurricane Blanca">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg"><img alt="Blanca 2015-06-03 2025Z.jpg" data-file-height="3210" data-file-width="2250" height="214" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg/150px-Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg/225px-Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg/300px-Blanca_2015-06-03_2025Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Blanca_2015_track.png"><img alt="Blanca 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Blanca_2015_track.png/150px-Blanca_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Blanca_2015_track.png/225px-Blanca_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/Blanca_2015_track.png/300px-Blanca_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>May 31 – June 9</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  936 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Blanca_(2015)" title="Hurricane Blanca (2015)">Hurricane Blanca (2015)</a></div>
<p>A tropical wave first monitored by the NHC late on May 27 spawned a weak area of low pressure well south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acapulco,_Mexico" title="Acapulco, Mexico">Acapulco, Mexico</a> two days later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup> Plagued by strong upper-level winds from Hurricane Andres, the disturbance slowly organized into the season's second tropical depression at 22:30 UTC on May 31 and further into Tropical Storm Blanca the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup> Moving little within a weak steering regime, the cyclone began <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a> by June 2 under favorable conditions aloft; at 21:00 UTC, it was upgraded to a Category 1 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlancaD9_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-BlancaD9-9">[8]</a></sup> Following the appearance of a pinhole eye,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BlancaD12_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-BlancaD12-10">[9]</a></sup> Blanca was upgraded to a Category 4 hurricane at 12:00 UTC on June 3. Shortly thereafter, Blanca reached its peak intensity with winds of 145 mph (230 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup> Tremendous <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">upwelling</a> of cooler waters, with some areas falling from 30 to 21 °C (86 to 70 °F),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WundergroundJune8_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-WundergroundJune8-41">[40]</a></sup> resulted in weakening early on June 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> Its eye quickly collapsed and convection diminished as it underwent an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup> Reconnaissance aircraft flew into the storm on June 5 and found Blanca to have degraded to Category 1 status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> The next day, Blanca rapidly reintensified and reached its secondary peak as a Category 4 with winds of 130 mph (215 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> Thereafter, cooler waters and southeasterly wind shear prompted a weakening phase once more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> After weakening to a tropical storm on June 7,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup> Blanca made <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landfall_(meteorology)" title="Landfall (meteorology)">landfall</a> around 12:00 UTC on June 8, near <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Cort%C3%A9s,_Baja_California_Sur" title="Puerto Cortés, Baja California Sur">Puerto Cortés</a> with winds of 45 mph (75 km/h) and became the earliest instance of a landfall in the <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Peninsula" title="Baja California Peninsula">Baja California Peninsula</a> since records began in 1949.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WundergroundJune8_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-WundergroundJune8-41">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> Thereafter, Blanca weakened to a tropical depression before degenerating into a remnant low early on June 9 as convection diminished.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup></p>
<p>On June 3, precautionary alerts were raised across the southern Baja California Peninsula and much of Western Mexico, due to potential impacts from the hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup> A collective 3,300 troops from the Mexican Army and Navy were deployed to <a href="/wiki/Baja_California_Sur" title="Baja California Sur">Baja California Sur</a> to ensure the safety of residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[51]</a></sup> Although Blanca remained far from <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a>, large <a href="/wiki/Swell_(ocean)" title="Swell (ocean)">swells</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rip_current" title="Rip current">rip currents</a> produced by the hurricane claimed four lives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> Across Baja California Sur, high winds downed power lines and left 104,106 residents without electricity. However, around 90 percent of the outages were fixed within 12 hours of the storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup> The remnants of Blanca later brought much-needed rain to parts of <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a>. Daily rainfall records were broken in several areas, though accumulations were generally less than 1 in (25 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Some flooding took place in <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_County,_California" title="Santa Barbara County, California">Santa Barbara County</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[55]</a></sup> Damage across the state amounted to $67,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> Additionally, on June 10, some of Blanca's moisture moved north and brought light showers to the <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">San Francisco Bay Area</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[57]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Carlos">Hurricane Carlos</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Hurricane Carlos">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg"><img alt="Carlos 2015-06-13 1755Z.jpg" data-file-height="2502" data-file-width="2085" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg/150px-Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg/225px-Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg/300px-Carlos_2015-06-13_1755Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Carlos_2015_track.png"><img alt="Carlos 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Carlos_2015_track.png/150px-Carlos_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Carlos_2015_track.png/225px-Carlos_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Carlos_2015_track.png/300px-Carlos_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>June 10 – June 17</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>90 mph (150 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  978 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Carlos_(2015)" title="Hurricane Carlos (2015)">Hurricane Carlos (2015)</a></div>
<p>In early June, a Kelvin wave interacted with a few tropical waves to the south of Mexico. The system gradually organized and was designated as a tropical depression on June 10, while situated about 290 mi (470 km) south-southeast of <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Escondido,_Oaxaca" title="Puerto Escondido, Oaxaca">Puerto Escondido, Oaxaca</a>. Drifting slowly northwestward, the depression was upgraded further to tropical storm intensity. Although persistent wind shear and dry air hampered intensification early on, Carlos strengthened into a hurricane on June 13 after moving into more favorable conditions. However, the return of dry air and upwelling caused the storm to deteriorate into a tropical storm. Paralleling the Mexican coast, Carlos regained hurricane intensity on June 15 and peaked with sustained winds of 90 mph (150 km/h) the next day. Wind shear and dry air afterwards led to rapid weakening, falling to tropical storm intensity on June 17 and degeneration into a remnant area of low pressure hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-59">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carlos' formation prompted coastal authorities to enact precautionary measures along states deemed at risk. In <a href="/wiki/Guerrero" title="Guerrero">Guerrero</a>, 507 shelters were opened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OK_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-OK-60">[59]</a></sup> The NHC also issued several <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_warnings_and_watches" title="Tropical cyclone warnings and watches">tropical cyclone warnings and watches</a> between June 11 and June 17 from <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a> to Guerrero. Rough seas along the shore generated by the hurricane caused widespread damage,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-59">[58]</a></sup> which included the sinking of 12 ships in Playa Manzanillo harbor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> The waves combined with heavy rain to inflict at least 5 million pesos (US$320,000) of damage on <a href="/wiki/Michoac%C3%A1n" title="Michoacán">Michoacán</a>'s coastal installations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ctcr_59-2"><a href="#cite_note-ctcr-59">[58]</a></sup> Strong winds produced by the passing storm also downed trees, power poles, and billboards, especially in Acapulco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[61]</a></sup> There, 16 homes were swept away by the waves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MN_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-MN-63">[62]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Ela">Tropical Storm Ela</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Ela">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg"><img alt="Ela 2015-07-09 2315Z.jpg" data-file-height="7905" data-file-width="6177" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg/150px-Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg/225px-Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg/300px-Ela_2015-07-09_2315Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ela_2015_track.png"><img alt="Ela 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Ela_2015_track.png/150px-Ela_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Ela_2015_track.png/225px-Ela_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Ela_2015_track.png/300px-Ela_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 8 – July 10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>45 mph (75 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave crossing the eastern Pacific spawned an area of low pressure on July 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ela_tcr_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ela_tcr-64">[63]</a></sup> The system gradually organized amid persistent wind shear and on July 8, the system intensified into Tropical Depression Four-E just before it entered the area of responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a> (CPHC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup> On July 9, the depression intensified into a tropical storm as it tracked to the northwest, and was named <i>Ela</i> by the CPHC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ela_tcr_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ela_tcr-64">[63]</a></sup> Ela intensified slightly to reach its peak intensity with 45 mph (75 km/h), however, strong wind shear prevented Ela from intensifying further by removing thunderstorms from the circulation center, in fact causing it to gradually weaken.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ela_tcr_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ela_tcr-64">[63]</a></sup> Eventually, Ela was downgraded into a depression on July 8, before being declared a remnant low well east of the <a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_Islands" title="Hawaiian Islands">Hawaiian Islands</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ela_tcr_64-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ela_tcr-64">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Ela is one of just six tropical cyclones to form as a depression in the east Pacific basin but not be named until entering the central Pacific; the others are <a href="/wiki/1984_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Lala" title="1984 Pacific hurricane season">Lala</a>, <a href="/wiki/1994_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Li" title="1994 Pacific hurricane season">Li</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Iniki" title="Hurricane Iniki">Iniki</a> and <a href="/wiki/2009_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Lana" title="2009 Pacific hurricane season">Lana</a>. It would be succeeded by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ulika" title="Hurricane Ulika">Hurricane Ulika</a> a year later. It is also the fourth earliest storm to form during the calendar year in the central Pacific after <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ekeka" title="Hurricane Ekeka">Ekeka</a> and <a href="/wiki/1992_Pacific_hurricane_season#Tropical_Storm_Hali" title="1992 Pacific hurricane season">Hali</a> of 1992,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TWC_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-TWC-67">[66]</a></sup> as well as <a href="/wiki/2016_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Pali" title="2016 Pacific hurricane season">Pali</a> of 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Halola">Tropical Storm Halola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Halola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg"><img alt="Halola 2015-07-13 0125Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg/150px-Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg/225px-Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg/300px-Halola_2015-07-13_0125Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Halola_2015_track.png"><img alt="Halola 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Halola_2015_track.png/150px-Halola_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Halola_2015_track.png/225px-Halola_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Halola_2015_track.png/300px-Halola_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 10 – July 12 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Halola_.28Goring.29" title="2015 Pacific typhoon season">exited basin</a>)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  998 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Typhoon_Halola" title="Typhoon Halola">Typhoon Halola</a></div>
<p>A tropical disturbance well to the southwest of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> organized into Tropical Depression One-C by July 10.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> Early the next day, the system developed into Tropical Storm Halola. On July 12, Halola crossed the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> and entered the Western Pacific basin, the area of responsibility of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Meteorological_Agency" title="Japan Meteorological Agency">Japan Meteorological Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Iune">Tropical Storm Iune</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Iune">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg"><img alt="Iune Jul 11 2015 2140Z.jpg" data-file-height="4800" data-file-width="3600" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg/150px-Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg/225px-Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg/300px-Iune_Jul_11_2015_2140Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Iune_2015_track.png"><img alt="Iune 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Iune_2015_track.png/150px-Iune_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Iune_2015_track.png/225px-Iune_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Iune_2015_track.png/300px-Iune_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 10 – July 13</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1003 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">On July 10, a tropical disturbance organized and became Tropical Depression Two-C. Due to an increase of convection near its centre, the CPHC upgraded the system to Tropical Storm Iune by the next day. But because of its small size and the upper level winds, Iune's circulation became exposed and had weakened to a tropical depression on July 12.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> By July 13, Iune degenerated to a remnant low as its remnant circulation moved in a slow westward direction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Dolores">Hurricane Dolores</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hurricane Dolores">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg"><img alt="Dolores 2015-07-15 1755Z.jpg" data-file-height="9400" data-file-width="7200" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg/150px-Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg/225px-Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg/300px-Dolores_2015-07-15_1755Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dolores_2015_track.png"><img alt="Dolores 2015 track.png" data-file-height="2020" data-file-width="3000" height="101" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Dolores_2015_track.png/150px-Dolores_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Dolores_2015_track.png/225px-Dolores_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Dolores_2015_track.png/300px-Dolores_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 11 – July 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>130 mph (215 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  946 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A westward-moving tropical wave crossed Central America and entered the Eastern Pacific. On July 11, the system was declared Tropical Depression Five-E. Despite moderate northwesterly wind shear, the depression quickly strengthened into Tropical Storm Dolores and reached hurricane status early on July 13. A day later, when the shear diminished, Dolores <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapidly intensified</a> into a Category 4 hurricane with winds 130 mph (215 km/h) and a minimum pressure of 946 mbar (hPa; 27.94 inHg). However, as Dolores approached <a href="/wiki/Socorro_Island" title="Socorro Island">Socorro Island</a>, the cyclone underwent an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a> and began to steadily weaken. By the morning of July 17, Dolores had deteriorated to a tropical storm, and eventually degenerated into a post-tropical remnant low about 300 miles west of the Baja California coast the next day. The remnant low slowly curved southwards and dissipated on 22 July west of <a href="/wiki/San_Diego" title="San Diego">San Diego, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[71]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ep052015tcr_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-ep052015tcr-73">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>Moisture extending from the storm's remnants brought record rains and thunderstorms to Southern California; record monthly rainfall totals include 2 in (51 mm) in San Diego, 1.30 in (33 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, and 1.16 in (29 mm) in <a href="/wiki/Paso_Robles,_California" title="Paso Robles, California">Paso Robles</a>. In the foothills and mountains of east <a href="/wiki/San_Diego_County,_California" title="San Diego County, California">San Diego County</a> (e.g. the town of <a href="/wiki/Ramona,_California" title="Ramona, California">Ramona</a>), rainfall exceeded 4 in (100 mm).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup> This had the effect of helping firefighters contain the <a href="/wiki/North_Fire" title="North Fire">North Fire</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> but also resulted in debris flows and rock slides that damaged about 90 homes and submerged cars,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ep052015tcr_73-1"><a href="#cite_note-ep052015tcr-73">[72]</a></sup> and washed out a bridge along <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10_in_California" title="Interstate 10 in California">Interstate 10</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup> The San Diego River reached levels of 8.9 ft (2.7 m)—just below flood stage—and overflowed its banks in a few areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ep052015tcr_73-2"><a href="#cite_note-ep052015tcr-73">[72]</a></sup> Flash flooding in <a href="/wiki/Riverside_County,_California" title="Riverside County, California">Riverside County</a> washed out a portion of <a href="/wiki/Interstate_10" title="Interstate 10">Interstate 10</a> and a bridge; losses reached $50 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Enrique">Tropical Storm Enrique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Enrique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="Enrique 2015-07-14 2155Z (cropped).jpg" data-file-height="5890" data-file-width="5220" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/150px-Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/225px-Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_%28cropped%29.jpg/300px-Enrique_2015-07-14_2155Z_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Enrique_2015_track.png"><img alt="Enrique 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Enrique_2015_track.png/150px-Enrique_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Enrique_2015_track.png/225px-Enrique_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Enrique_2015_track.png/300px-Enrique_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 12 – July 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1000 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave about 1,000 mi (1,610 km) southwest of the tip of the Baja California Peninsula spawned a broad area of low pressure on July 10. The low's circulation became increasingly well defined as the tropical wave moved away from the system, leading to the classification of Tropical Depression Six-E at 12:00 UTC on July 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnriqueTCR_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-EnriqueTCR-79">[78]</a></sup> Gradually organizing as it began to move west-northwestwards, the depression intensified to become Tropical Storm Enrique eighteen hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[79]</a></sup> Despite being situated in a generally favorable environment, dry air to the northwest of Enrique entrained into its circulation, thus Enrique struggled to intensify. Eventually, the system reached its peak intensity with 50 mph (85 km/h) winds and a minimum pressure of 1000 mbar (hPa; 29.53 inHg) late on July 14.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnriqueTCR_79-1"><a href="#cite_note-EnriqueTCR-79">[78]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[80]</a></sup> Thereafter, cooling sea surface temperatures and increasing southwesterly vertical wind shear took their toll on the cyclone, and Enrique started to weakened on July 15. Enrique continued to maintain its intensity over the next two days as it began to slow down and turn to the southwest under the influence of Hurricane Dolores to its east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnriqueTCR_79-2"><a href="#cite_note-EnriqueTCR-79">[78]</a></sup> However, during the afternoon of July 17, Enrique weakened to a tropical depression,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup> and further to a remnant low the next day. The remnants re-curved eastward over the next two days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EnriqueTCR_79-3"><a href="#cite_note-EnriqueTCR-79">[78]</a></sup> Throughout its lifetime, Enrique never affected land.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Felicia">Tropical Storm Felicia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Felicia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg"><img alt="Felicia 2015-07-23 1845Z.jpg" data-file-height="6400" data-file-width="5000" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg/150px-Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg/225px-Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg/300px-Felicia_2015-07-23_1845Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Felicia_2015_track.png"><img alt="Felicia 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Felicia_2015_track.png/150px-Felicia_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Felicia_2015_track.png/225px-Felicia_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Felicia_2015_track.png/300px-Felicia_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 23 – July 25</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1004 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A westward-tracking tropical wave moved off Africa on July 7, crossing into the East Pacific nine days later. The disturbance was initially disorganized, with a broad area of low pressure and intermittent convection; by 06:00 UTC on July 23, however, it acquired sufficient organization to be declared a tropical depression about 430 mi (690 km) southwest of the southern tip of Baja California.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FeliciaTCR_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-FeliciaTCR-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> Six hours later, the depression intensified into Tropical Storm Felicia and attained peak winds of 40 mph (65 km/h).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FeliciaTCR_84-1"><a href="#cite_note-FeliciaTCR-84">[83]</a></sup> The negative effects of shear, dry air, and cooler waters began to affect Felicia almost immediately, and the cyclone weakened to a tropical depression by 00:00 UTC on July 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FeliciaTCR_84-2"><a href="#cite_note-FeliciaTCR-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> All associated convection with the storm dissipated, marking Felicia's degeneration into a remnant low by 18:00 UTC that day. The low turned west and southwest prior to opening into a trough on July 28.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FeliciaTCR_84-3"><a href="#cite_note-FeliciaTCR-84">[83]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eight-E">Tropical Depression Eight-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eight-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg"><img alt="08E 2015-07-28 1900Z.jpg" data-file-height="5921" data-file-width="5073" height="175" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg/150px-08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg/225px-08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg/300px-08E_2015-07-28_1900Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08-E_2015_track.png"><img alt="08-E 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/08-E_2015_track.png/150px-08-E_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/08-E_2015_track.png/225px-08-E_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/08-E_2015_track.png/300px-08-E_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 27 – July 29</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1006 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A low pressure area formed in the middle of the Eastern Pacific. Moving northwest, the low slowly intensified into Tropical Depression Eight-E on July 27. However, strong north-northwesterly wind shear prevented it from intensifying into a tropical storm. As Eight-E moved into a drier environment, it failed to sustain deep convection near its center, and eventually degenerated into a remnant low early on July 30. Eight-E's remnants continued tracking in a westward direction and later crossed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">International Dateline</a> on August 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Guillermo">Hurricane Guillermo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Hurricane Guillermo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg"><img alt="Guillermo 2015-07-31 1935Z.jpg" data-file-height="7777" data-file-width="5809" height="201" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg/150px-Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg/225px-Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg/300px-Guillermo_2015-07-31_1935Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Guillermo_2015_track.png"><img alt="Guillermo 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Guillermo_2015_track.png/150px-Guillermo_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Guillermo_2015_track.png/225px-Guillermo_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/Guillermo_2015_track.png/300px-Guillermo_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>July 29 – August 7</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>110 mph (175 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  967 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical disturbance gained enough organization to be declared Tropical Depression Nine-E on July 29. Located in an environment of low wind shear, high sea surface temperatures and abundant moisture, conditions were very favorable for strengthening, allowing Nine-E to intensify into Tropical Storm Guillermo just 6 hours later. Continuing to quickly intensify, Guillermo became a hurricane only 36 hours after its formation, and eventually reached peak intensity with winds of 110 mph (175 km/h)—a strong Category 2 hurricane. Soon after, though, Guillermo weakened slightly, but remained at Category 2 strength as it crossed <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140°W</a> into the Central Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gtcr_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-gtcr-88">[87]</a></sup> However, as it neared <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, northeasterly wind shear began to weaken Guillermo,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> which eventually degraded to a tropical storm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> Despite restrengthening slightly on August 3,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> Guillermo soon resumed weakening and eventually degenerated into a post-tropical cyclone on August 7.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup></p>
<p>On August 6, some of Guillermo's moisture traveled to <a href="/wiki/Northern_California" title="Northern California">Northern California</a> and the San Francisco Bay Area to bring rare <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry_lightning" title="Dry lightning">dry lightning</a> storms to those areas during the night.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Hilda">Hurricane Hilda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Hurricane Hilda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg"><img alt="Hilda 2015-08-08 2025Z.jpg" data-file-height="6400" data-file-width="5000" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg/150px-Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg/225px-Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg/300px-Hilda_2015-08-08_2025Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hilda_2015_track.png"><img alt="Hilda 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hilda_2015_track.png/150px-Hilda_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hilda_2015_track.png/225px-Hilda_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Hilda_2015_track.png/300px-Hilda_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 5 – August 13</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  937 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave behind Guillermo gained enough organization to be declared Tropical Depression Ten-E. On August 6, the storm intensified into Tropical Storm Hilda. Amid moderate northeasterly wind shear and warm waters, Hilda gradually strengthened into a hurricane early on August 7. Rapid intensification ensued thereafter as the shear diminished, and Hilda became a Category 3 major hurricane just before entering the Central Pacific.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> Continuing to rapidly intensify, Hilda eventually reached its peak intensity as a Category 4 hurricane with 145 mph (230 km/h) sustained winds and a minimum pressure of 937 mbar (hPa).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> However, southwesterly shear from a nearby <a href="/wiki/Tropical_upper_tropospheric_trough" title="Tropical upper tropospheric trough">tropical upper tropospheric trough</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subtropical_jet_stream" title="Subtropical jet stream">subtropical jet stream</a> began to erode the system, and Hilda weakened back below major hurricane status on August 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Continuing to gradually weaken while approaching Hawaii, Hilda degraded to a tropical storm two days later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> and finally to a tropical depression on August 13.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> Hilda degenerated into a post-tropical cyclone late the same day,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> and dissipated early on August 14.</p>
<p>Hilda brought locally heavy rains to the <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Big Island</a>, though there were no reports of flooding.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eleven-E">Tropical Depression Eleven-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eleven-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg"><img alt="11E 2015-08-16 2130Z.jpg" data-file-height="6913" data-file-width="5281" height="196" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg/150px-11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg/225px-11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg/300px-11E_2015-08-16_2130Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:11-E_2015_track.png"><img alt="11-E 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/11-E_2015_track.png/150px-11-E_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/11-E_2015_track.png/225px-11-E_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/11-E_2015_track.png/300px-11-E_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 16 – August 18</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1003 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A broad area of low pressure around 485 miles (780 km) south-southwest of <a href="/wiki/Cabo_San_Lucas" title="Cabo San Lucas">Cabo San Lucas</a> organized into Tropical Depression Eleven-E on August 16. Moving on a northwesterly to west-northwesterly path, the cyclone failed to intensify and entered an area of unfavorable conditions late on August 17. Southeasterly shear, dry air entrainment and cooler waters caused the depression to lose its deep convection, eventually degenerating into a remnant low by August 18. The low turned to the north-northwest and dissipated 2 days later around 980 miles (1570 km) west of <a href="/wiki/Punta_Eugenia" title="Punta Eugenia">Punta Eugenia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Kilo">Hurricane Kilo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Hurricane Kilo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg"><img alt="Kilo 2015-08-29 2220Z.jpg" data-file-height="5665" data-file-width="4465" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg/150px-Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg/225px-Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg/300px-Kilo_2015-08-29_2220Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kilo_2015_track.png"><img alt="Kilo 2015 track.png" data-file-height="2110" data-file-width="2700" height="117" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kilo_2015_track.png/150px-Kilo_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kilo_2015_track.png/225px-Kilo_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Kilo_2015_track.png/300px-Kilo_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 20 – September 1 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Kilo" title="2015 Pacific typhoon season">Exited basin</a>)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>140 mph (220 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  940 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">On August 20, a low pressure area south of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> became Tropical Depression Three-C. The storm quickly strengthened into Tropical Storm Kilo and continued strengthening. The storm became a strong tropical storm, and despite being in a favorable environment, Kilo weakened into a Tropical Depression on August 23.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The storm would remain at tropical depression strength for the next three days.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">Despite its instability, Kilo's large-scale circulation brought enhanced moisture into Hawaii, leading to locally heavy rainfall in that state. After nearby Hurricane Loke moved north and dissipated on August 26, Kilo was able to restrengthen into a tropical storm. Intensification resumed the next day, with Kilo reaching hurricane strength. By August 29, Kilo had <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapidly intensified</a> into a major hurricane, as the storm neared the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>. Kilo peaked in intensity on August 30 as a Category 4 hurricane with winds of 140 miles per hour and a minimum central pressure of 940 millibars.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Kilo was also one of three simultaneous major hurricanes east of the International Date Line along with Ignacio and Jimena, the first such occurrence in recorded history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter.com_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iweathernet.com_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-iweathernet.com-14">[13]</a></sup> <span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">After peaking in strength, Kilo fluctuated between Category 3 and 4 strength as it slowly moved northwest, before slowly weakening below major hurricane status as conditions became less favorable.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It crossed the dateline early on September 1, becoming <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Kilo" title="2015 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Kilo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup> Kilo continued on to become one of the longest lived tropical cyclones on record, with a total lifespan of 22 days, just over 3 weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Loke">Hurricane Loke</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Hurricane Loke">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg"><img alt="Loke 2015-08-24 2200Z.jpg" data-file-height="8833" data-file-width="7297" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg/150px-Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg/225px-Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg/300px-Loke_2015-08-24_2200Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Loke_2015_track.png"><img alt="Loke 2015 track.png" data-file-height="2213" data-file-width="3000" height="111" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Loke_2015_track.png/150px-Loke_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Loke_2015_track.png/225px-Loke_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Loke_2015_track.png/300px-Loke_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>

<td>August 21 – August 26</td>

<td>75 mph (120 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  985 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>

<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>

<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(July 2016)</i></small></div>
</td>
