</table>
<p><span class="citation-needed-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">A tropical disturbance near the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Dateline" title="International Dateline">International Dateline</a> developed into Tropical Depression Four-C on August 21. Moving in an erratic northerly motion, the depression intensified into Tropical Storm Loke. Loke was upgraded to a minimal hurricane as it passed over the <a href="/wiki/Papah%C4%81naumoku%C4%81kea_Marine_National_Monument" title="Papahānaumokuākea Marine National Monument">Papahānaumokuākea Marine National Monument</a>. Soon after, Loke began accelerated north-northwestward as it neared the International Date Line. Loke became <a href="/wiki/Extratropical_cyclone" title="Extratropical cyclone">extratropical</a> late on August 26 as it crossed the basin. The storm was absorbed by <a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_typhoon_season#Typhoon_Atsani" title="2015 Pacific typhoon season">Typhoon Atsani</a> the day after.</span><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Ignacio">Hurricane Ignacio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Hurricane Ignacio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg"><img alt="Ignacio 2015-08-29 Suomi NPP.jpg" data-file-height="2147" data-file-width="1651" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Ignacio_2015-08-29_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ignacio_2015_track.png"><img alt="Ignacio 2015 track.png" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ignacio_2015_track.png/150px-Ignacio_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ignacio_2015_track.png/225px-Ignacio_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Ignacio_2015_track.png/300px-Ignacio_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 25 – September 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>145 mph (230 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  942 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On August 25, a low-pressure system formed and organized into Tropical Depression Twelve-E, before strengthening into Tropical Storm Ignacio.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IgnacioTCR_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-IgnacioTCR-105">[104]</a></sup> Ignacio initially moved west-northwest, posing a threat to Hawaii. On August 26, Ignacio became a Category 1 hurricane, while continuing its trek towards Hawaii. Over the next few days, Ignacio struggled to intensify while being impacted by moderate wind shear.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IgnacioTCR_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-IgnacioTCR-105">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup> As wind shear relaxed, Ignacio was able to quickly intensify to major hurricane status on August 29, attaining winds of 115 miles per hour. At this time, the Big Island of Hawaii was placed under a Tropical Storm Watch, as the island began feeling the effects of high surf.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> Ignacio continued to rapidly intensify, attaining peak intensity at Category 4 status with winds of 145 miles per hour and a minimum central pressure of 942 millibars on August 30.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> Ignacio was also one of three simultaneous Category 4 hurricanes east of the International Dateline along with Kilo and Jimena, the first such occurrence in recorded history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-twitter.com_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-twitter.com-13">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iweathernet.com_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-iweathernet.com-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>After peaking in intensity, Ignacio began weakening after moving into a less favorable environment. While weakening, Ignacio passed to the north of the Hawaii island chain, causing only minimal impacts. The storm weakened to tropical storm strength on September 1, but was able to reattain hurricane status. This would repeat once again, before the storm weakened to a tropical storm for the last time, and became post-tropical six hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> The remnants of Ignacio continued north across the Pacific, before turning to the northeast towards <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada" title="Western Canada">western Canada</a>. On September 8, the extratropical remnants of Ignacio moved <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia_Coast" title="British Columbia Coast">onshore in British Columbia</a>, bringing only light rain and few clouds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Jimena">Hurricane Jimena</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Hurricane Jimena">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg"><img alt="Jimena 2015-08-30 2250Z.jpg" data-file-height="2770" data-file-width="2003" height="207" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg/150px-Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg/225px-Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg/300px-Jimena_2015-08-30_2250Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jimena_2015_track.png"><img alt="Jimena 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jimena_2015_track.png/150px-Jimena_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jimena_2015_track.png/225px-Jimena_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Jimena_2015_track.png/300px-Jimena_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 26 – September 10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>155 mph (250 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  932 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A westward-moving low pressure area organized into a tropical depression on August 26, around 640 mi (1030 km) southwest of Manzanillo, Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup> The next day, the depression developed a tight inner core with sustained gale-force winds; accordingly, it was named <i>Jimena</i> by the NHC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> Moving over very warm waters near 30 °C (86 °F) and located in an environment of low wind shear and abundant moisture, Jimena underwent a period of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a> over the next 48 hours.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-1"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup> The NHC upgraded Jimena to a hurricane merely 30 hours after being named,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> and further to a major hurricane 18 hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Early on August 29, Jimena reached its peak intensity with winds of 155 mph (250 km/h)—just below Category 5 status on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir-Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" title="Saffir-Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir-Simpson hurricane wind scale</a>—and a minimum barometric pressure of 932 mbar (hPa; 27.52 inHg).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-2"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup> Soon after, Jimena turned to the west-northwest and underwent an <a href="/wiki/Eyewall_replacement_cycle" title="Eyewall replacement cycle">eyewall replacement cycle</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> Despite weakening slightly, Jimena remained at Category 4 status, thus becoming one of three simultaneous Category 4 major hurricanes east of the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a> on August 30—the first such occurrence of its kind.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-iweathernet.com_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-iweathernet.com-14">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early on August 31, Jimena completed the eyewall replacement cycle and quickly regained 150 mph (240 km/h) winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Upwelling" title="Upwelling">upwelling</a> of cooler waters beneath the hurricane and entrainment of mid-level dry air into the circulation, as well as a second eyewall replacement cycle, resulted in a steady weakening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-3"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup> The next day, Jimena crossed <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140°W</a> as a Category 3 hurricane and entered the jurisdiction of the CPHC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-4"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> Jimena continued to weaken slowly amid cooling sea surface temperatures and increasing northerly wind shear, eventually degrading below hurricane status on September 5.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-5"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup> Curving to the northwest, bursts of convection maintained Jimena as a tropical storm, in spite of westerly wind shear in excess of 20 knots causing the low-level circulation center to be exposed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> Devoid of deep convection near its center, Jimena eventually weakened to a tropical depression on September 9 as it turned west-southwestwards towards the Hawaiian islands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> Succumbing to the strong shear, Jimena degenerated into a remnant low and dissipated soon after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JimenaTCR_112-6"><a href="#cite_note-JimenaTCR-112">[111]</a></sup> Jimena never posed a threat to land, only bringing scattered heavy rains to Hawaii.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Kevin">Tropical Storm Kevin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Kevin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg"><img alt="Kevin 2015-09-03 2050Z.jpg" data-file-height="6400" data-file-width="5000" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg/150px-Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg/225px-Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg/300px-Kevin_2015-09-03_2050Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kevin_2015_track.png"><img alt="Kevin 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kevin_2015_track.png/150px-Kevin_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kevin_2015_track.png/225px-Kevin_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Kevin_2015_track.png/300px-Kevin_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>August 31 – September 5</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>60 mph (95 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  998 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave crossed Central America on August 25. Although it initially only produced transient bursts of convection, slow organization of the feature led to the formation of a tropical depression by 18:00 UTC on August 31 while located well south of Baja California. Steered northwest and the north-northwest, the cyclone intensified into Tropical Storm Kevin by 18:00 UTC the next day while being plagued by moderate wind shear. After reaching peak winds of 60 mph (95 km/h) on September 3, a further increase in upper-level winds caused the low- and mid-level circulations to become displaced. Devoid of deep convection, Kevin degenerated to a remnant low by 12:00 UTC on September 5; the remnant circulation drifted northwest and dissipated the following day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Linda">Hurricane Linda</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Hurricane Linda">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffc140">Category 3 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg"><img alt="Linda 2015-09-08 2110Z.jpg" data-file-height="9400" data-file-width="7400" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg/150px-Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg/225px-Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg/300px-Linda_2015-09-08_2110Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linda_2015_track.png"><img alt="Linda 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Linda_2015_track.png/150px-Linda_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Linda_2015_track.png/225px-Linda_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Linda_2015_track.png/300px-Linda_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 6 – September 10</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>125 mph (205 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  950 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Linda_(2015)" title="Hurricane Linda (2015)">Hurricane Linda (2015)</a></div>
<p>Early in September, a cluster of clouds began to organize into a tropical system. At 03:00 UTC on September 6, they organized enough to be called Tropical Depression Fifteen-E. Twelve hours later, the depression organized enough to be classified as a tropical storm and was given the name Linda. Linda rapidly strengthened as it moved on a northwestward course and became a hurricane just twelve hours after becoming a tropical storm due to large amounts of deep convection forming around the center. Linda then became a Category 2 hurricane. After stalling at Category 2 intensity, Linda again rapidly intensified, this time to a Category 3 major hurricane. Less than a day after becoming a major hurricane, Linda rapidly weakened due to increasing wind shear and decreasing water temperatures, becoming a remnant low less than a week after forming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup></p>
<p>Monsoonal moisture pulled north from Linda brought thunderstorms to portions of California. Flooding and rock slides prompted numerous road closures. One person drowned in the <a href="/wiki/San_Bernardino_National_Forest" title="San Bernardino National Forest">San Bernardino National Forest</a>. Remnants moisture from Linda with a weak cold front also caused record heavy rainfall in Los Angeles on September 15,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> with 3 swift water rescues and roughly 2 inches of rain across the L.A. basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to <a href="/wiki/San_Jose_State_University" title="San Jose State University">San Jose State University</a>, Linda's remnants may have also contributed to the severity of the <a href="/wiki/Valley_Fire" title="Valley Fire">Valley Fire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Malia">Tropical Storm Malia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Malia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg"><img alt="Malia 2015-09-20 0005Z.jpg" data-file-height="8513" data-file-width="6817" height="187" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg/150px-Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg/225px-Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg/300px-Malia_2015-09-20_0005Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Malia_2015_track.png"><img alt="Malia 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Malia_2015_track.png/150px-Malia_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Malia_2015_track.png/225px-Malia_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Malia_2015_track.png/300px-Malia_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 18 – September 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>50 mph (85 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  992 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(July 2016)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>After more than a week of inactivity, a tropical disturbance intensified into Tropical Depression Five-C east of the International Dateline on September 19. The depression moved north-northeast, before it crossed <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> and was upgraded to Tropical Storm Malia on September 21. However, Malia weakened into a post-tropical cyclone on the next day, shortly before being absorbed into a frontal system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malia_tcr_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-Malia_tcr-130">[129]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Sixteen-E">Tropical Depression Sixteen-E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Sixteen-E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg"><img alt="16E 2015-09-20 1820Z.jpg" data-file-height="6273" data-file-width="5009" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg/150px-16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg/225px-16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg/300px-16E_2015-09-20_1820Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:16-E_2015_track.png"><img alt="16-E 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/16-E_2015_track.png/150px-16-E_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/16-E_2015_track.png/225px-16-E_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/16-E_2015_track.png/300px-16-E_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 20 – September 21</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1001 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave gained enough organization to be declared Tropical Depression Sixteen-E on September 20. Located in an environment of strong southerly shear, the depression failed to intensify into a tropical storm. The next day, the heavily sheared system made landfall on Baja California, then on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isla_Tiburon" title="Isla Tiburon">Isla Tiburon</a>, and finally in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sonora,_Mexico" title="Sonora, Mexico">Sonora, Mexico</a>. It dissipated just hours later, with its remnants going on to affect parts of Arizona and New Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16E_tcr_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-16E_tcr-131">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>Widespread heavy rains in Baja California and Sonora caused heavy flooding. Preliminary damage estimates in <a href="/wiki/El_Fuerte,_Sinaloa" title="El Fuerte, Sinaloa">El Fuerte, Sinaloa</a>, reached 300 million pesos (US$17.7 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16E_tcr_131-1"><a href="#cite_note-16E_tcr-131">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> The remnant low brought considerable moisture to the Desert Southwest, and later combined with other systems to produce flooding across the <a href="/wiki/Great_Plains" title="Great Plains">Great Plains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upper_Midwest" title="Upper Midwest">Upper Midwest</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16E_tcr_131-2"><a href="#cite_note-16E_tcr-131">[130]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16Etwc_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-16Etwc-133">[132]</a></sup> Rainfall in <a href="/wiki/Roswell,_New_Mexico" title="Roswell, New Mexico">Roswell, New Mexico</a>, reached 3 in (76 mm). One person drowned along the <a href="/wiki/Rio_Grande" title="Rio Grande">Rio Grande</a> in New Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> Flooding also took place near <a href="/wiki/Phoenix,_Arizona" title="Phoenix, Arizona">Phoenix, Arizona</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16Etwc_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-16Etwc-133">[132]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Niala">Tropical Storm Niala</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Niala">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg"><img alt="Niala 2015-09-25 2020Z.jpg" data-file-height="6529" data-file-width="5137" height="191" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg/150px-Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg/225px-Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg/300px-Niala_2015-09-25_2020Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Niala_2015_track.png"><img alt="Niala 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Niala_2015_track.png/150px-Niala_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Niala_2015_track.png/225px-Niala_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Niala_2015_track.png/300px-Niala_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 25 – September 28</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>65 mph (100 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  992 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 20, a tropical disturbance was identified southeast of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a>, moving westward south of the <a href="/wiki/Subtropical_ridge" title="Subtropical ridge">subtropical ridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> The disturbance organized, a which led to the formation of Tropical Depression Six-C on September 25.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-1"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> It was upgraded into Tropical Storm Niala soon after, and the storm headed west-northwest towards Hawaii.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-2"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> Niala reached its peak intensity with winds of 65 mph, and a pressure of 992 mbars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-3"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> At this point, Tropical Storm Warnings were issued for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Big_Island_of_Hawaii" title="Big Island of Hawaii">Big Island</a>, as were High Surf &amp; Marine Advisories for the same area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-4"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> Throughout September 26, forecasts called for a westwards turn, just barely missing the Big Island. The next day, however, it became evident that Niala was turning more towards the southwest by being steered by the lower level winds, sparing Hawaii from landfall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-5"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> At this time, Niala dropped to 50 mph winds, and subsequently degraded into a depression on the 28th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-6"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup> Later that day, unfavorable conditions including high wind shear weakened the storm even more, and Niala degenerated into a post-tropical remnant low late at 0000 UTC on September 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> The remnant low continued westwards, dissipating early October 1.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Niala_tcr_135-7"><a href="#cite_note-Niala_tcr-135">[134]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Marty">Hurricane Marty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Hurricane Marty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffffcc">Category 1 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg"><img alt="Marty 2015-09-28 1735Z.jpg" data-file-height="7800" data-file-width="6000" height="195" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg/150px-Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg/225px-Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg/300px-Marty_2015-09-28_1735Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marty_2015_track.png"><img alt="Marty 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Marty_2015_track.png/150px-Marty_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Marty_2015_track.png/225px-Marty_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Marty_2015_track.png/300px-Marty_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>September 26 – September 30</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>80 mph (130 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  987 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Marty_(2015)" title="Hurricane Marty (2015)">Hurricane Marty (2015)</a></div>
<p>A tropical wave, the northern portion of which led to the formation of the Atlantic's <a href="/wiki/2015_Atlantic_hurricane_season#Tropical_Depression_Nine" title="2015 Atlantic hurricane season">Tropical Depression Nine</a>, emerged off the western coast of Africa on September 10. Steered steadily westward, the wave entered the East Pacific where deep convection coalesced around a well-defined center; this led to the formation of a tropical depression about 335 mi (540 km) southwest of Acapulco, Mexico by 18:00 UTC on September 26. The depression intensified into Tropical Storm Marty six hours later as it drifted north. Amid an environment conducive for strengthening, Marty reached hurricane intensity at 12:00 UTC on September 28 and attained peak winds of 80 mph (130 km/h) shortly thereafter. Wind shear abruptly increased following peak intensity, causing the cyclone to weaken quickly; it was downgraded to a tropical storm at 06:00 UTC on September 29 and degenerated into a remnant low a day later. The low eventually dissipated south of the Mexico coastline on October 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup></p>
<p>Heavy rains and flooding from the remnants of Marty rendered 35,000 people homeless in <a href="/wiki/Sonora" title="Sonora">Sonora</a>. Flooding in <a href="/wiki/Guaymas" title="Guaymas">Guaymas</a> damaged 800 homes and 400 vehicles; three people sustained injuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Oho">Hurricane Oho</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Hurricane Oho">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ffe775">Category 2 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg"><img alt="Oho 2015-10-06 2310Z.jpg" data-file-height="7521" data-file-width="5681" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg/150px-Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg/225px-Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg/300px-Oho_2015-10-06_2310Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Oho_2015_track.png"><img alt="Oho 2015 track.png" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="3000" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Oho_2015_track.png/150px-Oho_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Oho_2015_track.png/225px-Oho_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Oho_2015_track.png/300px-Oho_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 3 – October 8</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>110 mph (175 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  957 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In an uncommon occurrence, a slow moving disturbance detached from a monsoon trough southeast of Hawaii and became Tropical Depression Seven-C on October 3.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-0"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> With a favorable environment, the storm became Tropical Storm Oho quickly after.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-1"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> With this, Oho became the record breaking twelfth storm this year to enter, or form in the Central Pacific. Under southwesterly wind shear, Oho slowly intensified while accelerating northeastwards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-2"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> While tracking northeastward, Oho became a Category 2 on October 7, attaining peak intensity of 110 mph and a pressure of 957 mbars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-3"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> Shortly after its peak, Oho moved to an area with cooler ocean temperatures and increasing southwesterly wind shear, which caused the storm to weaken and to lose its tropcal characteristics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-4"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> The storm became extratropical on October 8 and briefly weakened to a gale low on early October 9.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-5"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> However, due to strong baroclinicity, Ex-Oho briefly re-attained hurricane-force winds before starting a stead weakening.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-6"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup> On October 10, Oho's remnants moved into Alaska as a moderate extratropical storm, where it weakened, until the system dissipated over western Canada 6 hours later.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Oho_tcr_139-7"><a href="#cite_note-Oho_tcr-139">[138]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Eight-C">Tropical Depression Eight-C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Eight-C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg"><img alt="08C 2015-10-04 2155Z.jpg" data-file-height="6689" data-file-width="5281" height="190" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg/150px-08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg/225px-08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg/300px-08C_2015-10-04_2155Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:08-C_2015_track.png"><img alt="08-C 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/08-C_2015_track.png/150px-08-C_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/08-C_2015_track.png/225px-08-C_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/08-C_2015_track.png/300px-08-C_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 3 – October 4 <small>(<a href="/wiki/2015_Pacific_typhoon_season#Other_storms" title="2015 Pacific typhoon season">Exited basin on October 6</a>)</small></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1001 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>On September 30, a tropical disturbance well east of the International Dateline developed from a monsoon trough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8E_tcr_141-0"><a href="#cite_note-8E_tcr-141">[140]</a></sup> Slowly organizing, the CPHC started to issue advisories on it as a tropical depression and designated it as Eight-C.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8E_tcr_141-1"><a href="#cite_note-8E_tcr-141">[140]</a></sup> Shortly after however, southerly wind shear inhibited the storm to intensify to a tropical storm and caused its convection to collapse.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8E_tcr_141-2"><a href="#cite_note-8E_tcr-141">[140]</a></sup> With the low-level closed circulation being displaced to the south of the remnant convection, the CPHC issued its final advisory on the next day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8E_tcr_141-3"><a href="#cite_note-8E_tcr-141">[140]</a></sup> Eight-C's remnants slowly drifted west-northwestward until late on October 6, Eight-C crossed the basin and the Japan Meteorological Agency started warning on it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8E_tcr_141-4"><a href="#cite_note-8E_tcr-141">[140]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Nora">Tropical Storm Nora</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Nora">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>

<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg"><img alt="Nora 2015-10-11 2020Z.jpg" data-file-height="6833" data-file-width="5329" height="192" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg/150px-Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg/225px-Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg/300px-Nora_2015-10-11_2020Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nora_2015_track.png"><img alt="Nora 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Nora_2015_track.png/150px-Nora_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Nora_2015_track.png/225px-Nora_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Nora_2015_track.png/300px-Nora_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>

<td>October 9 – October 15</td>

<td>70 mph (110 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  993 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg"><img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text">
<div class="mbox-text-span"><b>This section needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small> <small><i>(July 2016)</i></small></div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A westward moving disturbance became Tropical Depression Eighteen-E on October 9. Steadily moving westwards, the depression became Tropical Storm Nora soon after. Curving west-northwestwards, Nora continued to intensify and was forecast to attain hurricane strength. After crossing into the Central Pacific, Nora peaked with winds of 70 mph and a pressure of 993 millibars. Continuing northwestwards, Nora encountering less favorable conditions and quickly weakened, dissipating on October 15.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Olaf">Hurricane Olaf</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Hurricane Olaf">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg"><img alt="Olaf 2015-10-20 Suomi NPP.jpg" data-file-height="2995" data-file-width="2085" height="215" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Olaf_2015-10-20_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Olaf_2015_track.png"><img alt="Olaf 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1867" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Olaf_2015_track.png/150px-Olaf_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Olaf_2015_track.png/225px-Olaf_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Olaf_2015_track.png/300px-Olaf_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 15 – October 27</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 mph (240 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  938 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Olaf originated from a broad low pressure area that formed late on October 10. At first, it showed some signs of organization, but convection associated with the system soon diminished due to temporary unfavorable conditions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup> Eventually the system reorganized, and by October 15, it had gained enough organization to be designated as Tropical Depression Nineteen-E.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> Despite very favorable conditions, the system did not organize at first, maintaining its intensity for two days. Finally, the system's organization improved, and the NHC named the depression <i>Olaf</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> Soon after, Olaf began to rapidly intensify and became a hurricane on October 18, with hints of an eye starting to appear within organized deep convection. Located at just 9.3°N, it broke the record for the lowest-latitude hurricane formation in the eastern Pacific basin since reliable records began in 1971.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-1"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> Olaf's intensification rate increased, and the next day, Olaf had become a major hurricane with a well-defined pinhole eye. At 9.8°N, it broke the record for the lowest-latitude major hurricane formation in the eastern Pacific basin as well.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-2"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> Six hours later, Olaf was upgraded to a Category 4 hurricane, the eighth of the season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> Moving west-northwestwards, Olaf reached peak intensity with 150 mph (240 km/h) winds and a pressure of 938 mbar (hPa; 27.70 inHg), just as it crossed into the Central Pacific basin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-3"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Maintaining peak intensity for 12 hours, Olaf weakened due to an eyewall replacement cycle, falling down to a low-end Category 3 hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-4"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup> Although the eye appeared on satellite again, cloud tops warmed, and Olaf weakened below major hurricane status while getting recurved to the north by a passing trough. However, despite only partially favorable conditions cloud tops associated with Olaf cooled again and Olaf reached a secondary peak intensity of 120 mph (195 km/h). Decreasing sea surface temperatures and vertical wind shear finally began to weaken the storm for good, and although an eye could still be made out on satellite until October 25, the convective structure of Olaf began to degrade. Following dissipation of the eye, Olaf was downgraded to a tropical storm on October 25. The trough had now begun to pull Olaf to the east, and Olaf then re-entered the eastern Pacific basin on October 26, becoming the first storm on record to cross into the Central Pacific and turn back into the Eastern Pacific while still a tropical cyclone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-5"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> The last of Olaf's deep convection continued to be sheared away, and Olaf was downgraded to a remnant low later on the same day, although the system was still producing gale-force winds. Olaf's remnant low gradually weakened, before dissipating on October 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OlafTCR_143-6"><a href="#cite_note-OlafTCR-143">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p>Although <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_Storm_Ema" title="Tropical Storm Ema">Tropical Storm Ema</a> in <a href="/wiki/1982_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1982 Pacific hurricane season">1982</a> also crossed from the central Pacific to the eastern Pacific, Olaf is notable for being only one of two tropical cyclones to ever re-enter the eastern Pacific after moving into the central Pacific; the other being <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hurricane_Ulika" title="Hurricane Ulika">Hurricane Ulika</a>.</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Hurricane Patricia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff6060">Category 5 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg"><img alt="Patricia 2015-10-23 1730Z.jpg" data-file-height="8000" data-file-width="6000" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg/150px-Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg/225px-Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg/300px-Patricia_2015-10-23_1730Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Patricia_2015_track.png"><img alt="Patricia 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Patricia_2015_track.png/150px-Patricia_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Patricia_2015_track.png/225px-Patricia_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Patricia_2015_track.png/300px-Patricia_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>October 20 – October 24</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>215 mph (345 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  872 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Patricia" title="Hurricane Patricia">Hurricane Patricia</a></div>
<p>Tropical Depression Twenty-E formed on October 20, off the southwestern coast of Mexico. It only slowly intensified at first, becoming Tropical Storm Patricia later that day. It organized rapidly, beginning early on October 21, and became a hurricane late that day, in an atmosphere highly conducive to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rapid_deepening" title="Rapid deepening">rapid deepening</a>. On October 22, explosive intensification occurred, and in only 24 hours, Patricia became a Category 5 hurricane with 175 mph (280 km/h) winds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PatriciaTCR_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-PatriciaTCR-20">[19]</a></sup> The intensification rate rivaled those of <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Linda_(1997)" title="Hurricane Linda (1997)">Hurricane Linda</a> in <a href="/wiki/1997_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="1997 Pacific hurricane season">1997</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> in <a href="/wiki/2005_Atlantic_hurricane_season" title="2005 Atlantic hurricane season">2005</a>. Patricia subsequently attained winds of 215 mph (345 km/h) and a central pressure of 872 mbar (hPa; 25.75 inHg), becoming the strongest tropical cyclone ever recorded in the Western Hemisphere, surpassing both the previous central pressure record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Wilma" title="Hurricane Wilma">Hurricane Wilma</a> and the previous 1-minute sustained wind record set by <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Allen" title="Hurricane Allen">Hurricane Allen</a>. Patricia weakened even more rapidly than it intensified; just 30 hours after peaking in intensity, it was downgraded to a remnant low at 16:00 CDT on October 24.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> However, Patricia's landfall in Western Mexico as a Category 4 hurricane with winds of 150 mph (240 km/h), was still sufficient to qualify as the strongest landfall by any Pacific hurricane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PatriciaTCR_20-2"><a href="#cite_note-PatriciaTCR-20">[19]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Storm_Rick">Tropical Storm Rick</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tropical Storm Rick">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #00faf4">Tropical storm (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg"><img alt="Rick 2015-11-19 2015Z.jpg" data-file-height="5800" data-file-width="4600" height="189" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg/150px-Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg/225px-Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg/300px-Rick_2015-11-19_2015Z.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rick_2015_track.png"><img alt="Rick 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Rick_2015_track.png/150px-Rick_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Rick_2015_track.png/225px-Rick_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Rick_2015_track.png/300px-Rick_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 18 – November 22</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>40 mph (65 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1002 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>A tropical wave moved off the western coast of Africa on November 3, entering the East Pacific roughly two weeks later. The disturbance encountered a persistent area of convection in the ITCZ, eventually coalescing into a tropical depression by 12:00 UTC on November 18 while located 715 mi (1,150 km) south-southeast of the southern tip of Baja California. Plagued by moderate southeasterly wind shear, the depression slowly intensified into Tropical Storm Rick and simultaneously attained peak winds of 40 mph (65 km/h) by 12:00 UTC on November 19. The cyclone failed to intensify further as it tracked west-northwest within a dry environment, weakening to a tropical depression by 06:00 UTC on November 22 and further degenerating into a remnant low twelve hours later. The low tracked northwest and eventually southwest prior to dissipating early on November 26.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hurricane_Sandra">Hurricane Sandra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Hurricane Sandra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #ff8f20">Category 4 hurricane (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg"><img alt="Sandra 2015-11-25 Suomi NPP.jpg" data-file-height="3336" data-file-width="2502" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg/150px-Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg/225px-Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg/300px-Sandra_2015-11-25_Suomi_NPP.jpg 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sandra_2015_track.png"><img alt="Sandra 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1669" data-file-width="2700" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Sandra_2015_track.png/150px-Sandra_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Sandra_2015_track.png/225px-Sandra_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Sandra_2015_track.png/300px-Sandra_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>November 23 – November 28</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>150 mph (240 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  934 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hurricane_Sandra_(2015)" title="Hurricane Sandra (2015)">Hurricane Sandra (2015)</a></div>
<p>Originating from a <a href="/wiki/Tropical_wave" title="Tropical wave">tropical wave</a> that emerged off the west coast of Africa on November 6, Sandra was first classified as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tropical_depression" title="Tropical depression">tropical depression</a> on November 23 well south of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>. Environmental conditions, including high <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sea_surface_temperatures" title="Sea surface temperatures">sea surface temperatures</a> and low <a href="/wiki/Wind_shear" title="Wind shear">wind shear</a>, were highly conducive to intensification and the storm quickly organized. A small <a href="/wiki/Central_dense_overcast" title="Central dense overcast">central dense overcast</a> developed atop the storm and Sandra reached hurricane status early on November 25 after the consolidation of an <a href="/wiki/Eye_(cyclone)" title="Eye (cyclone)">eye</a>. The hurricane achieved its peak as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SSHS#Category_4" title="SSHS">Category 4</a> hurricane with winds of 150 mph (240 km/h) and a pressure of 934 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>; 27.58 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inches_of_Mercury" title="Inches of Mercury">inHg</a>) early on November 26. This made Sandra the strongest November hurricane on record in the Northeastern Pacific, surpassing <a href="/wiki/2011_Pacific_hurricane_season#Hurricane_Kenneth" title="2011 Pacific hurricane season">Hurricane Kenneth</a> in 2011. Thereafter, increasing shear degraded the hurricane's structure and weakening ensued. Rapid weakening took place on November 27 and Sandra's circulation became devoid of <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_convection" title="Atmospheric convection">convection</a> as it diminished to a tropical storm that evening. The cyclone degenerated into a remnant low soon thereafter and ultimately dissipated just off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Sinaloa" title="Sinaloa">Sinaloa</a>, Mexico, on November 29.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SandraTCR_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-SandraTCR-21">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the precursor to Sandra traversed <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">Central America</a>, it produced unseasonably heavy rainfall that triggered flooding and landslides. Four people died in various incidents related to the system: three in <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a> and one in <a href="/wiki/Honduras" title="Honduras">Honduras</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> Initially expecting a <a href="/wiki/Landfall" title="Landfall">landfalling</a> storm, officials in Northwestern Mexico prepared equipment for power outages, closed schools, and evacuated 180 residents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> Sandra's effects largely consisted of light to moderate rainfall; some traffic accidents and landslides resulted from this, though the overall impacts were limited.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SandraTCR_21-2"><a href="#cite_note-SandraTCR-21">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tropical_Depression_Nine-C">Tropical Depression Nine-C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Tropical Depression Nine-C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 24em;">
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-weight: bold; background: #5ebaff">Tropical depression (SSHWS)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
<div style="vertical-align: middle"><span class="nowrap"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png"><img alt="09C 2015-12-31 Suomi NPP.png" data-file-height="3336" data-file-width="2502" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png/150px-09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png/225px-09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png/300px-09C_2015-12-31_Suomi_NPP.png 2x" width="150"/></a><span class="nowrap"> </span><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:09-C_2015_track.png"><img alt="09-C 2015 track.png" data-file-height="1854" data-file-width="3000" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/09-C_2015_track.png/150px-09-C_2015_track.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/09-C_2015_track.png/225px-09-C_2015_track.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/09-C_2015_track.png/300px-09-C_2015_track.png 2x" width="150"/></a></span></div>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Duration</th>
<td>December 31 – December 31</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row">Peak intensity</th>
<td>35 mph (55 km/h) <small>(1-min)</small>  1001 <a href="/wiki/Bar_(unit)" title="Bar (unit)">mbar</a> (<a href="/wiki/Pascal_(unit)" title="Pascal (unit)">hPa</a>)</td>
</tr>
</table>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_off-season_Pacific_hurricanes" title="List of off-season Pacific hurricanes">List of off-season Pacific hurricanes</a></div>
<p>Despite the official end of the hurricane season about a month prior, the persistence of favorable environments in the Central Pacific lead to the development of a tropical disturbance on December 27.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9C_tcr_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-9C_tcr-155">[154]</a></sup> Moving slowly eastward, the disturbance stayed in an environment with ample ocean heat content, which led to the development and maintenance of the thunderstorms in this system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9C_tcr_155-1"><a href="#cite_note-9C_tcr-155">[154]</a></sup> Turning northwards, the system gained latitude and formed a low-level closed circulation, which led the CPHC to start advisories on Tropical Depression Nine-C at a very low latitude at 03:00 UTC on December 31.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9C_tcr_155-2"><a href="#cite_note-9C_tcr-155">[154]</a></sup> Moving slowly westwards, Nine-C never reached tropical storm strength due to its proximity to the equator and being under 20-knot vertical wind shear, leaving the 2015 season one storm shy of the record from 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9C_tcr_155-3"><a href="#cite_note-9C_tcr-155">[154]</a></sup> As convection diminished due to an area of deep convection that had been in the vicinity of Nine-C moving away from it, the depression was unable to support itself and was downgraded into a remnant low at 00:00 UTC on January 1, 2016, marking the latest end to a Pacific hurricane season on record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9C_tcr_155-4"><a href="#cite_note-9C_tcr-155">[154]</a></sup> The remant low dissipated later that day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9C_tcr_155-5"><a href="#cite_note-9C_tcr-155">[154]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Storm_names">Storm names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Storm names">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Tropical_cyclone_naming" title="Tropical cyclone naming">Tropical cyclone naming</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_tropical_cyclone_naming" title="History of tropical cyclone naming">History of tropical cyclone naming</a>, and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historic_tropical_cyclone_names" title="List of historic tropical cyclone names">List of historic tropical cyclone names</a></div>

The names not retired from this list will be used again in the 2021 season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCNames_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCNames-156">[155]</a></sup> This is the same list used in the <a href="/wiki/2009_Pacific_hurricane_season" title="2009 Pacific hurricane season">2009 season</a>.</p>

<p>For storms that form in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Pacific_Hurricane_Center" title="Central Pacific Hurricane Center">Central Pacific Hurricane Center</a>'s area of responsibility, encompassing the area between <a href="/wiki/140th_meridian_west" title="140th meridian west">140°W</a> and the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, all names are used in a series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_tropical_cyclone_names#Central_North_Pacific_.28140.C2.B0W_to_180.C2.B0.29" title="List of tropical cyclone names">four rotating lists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CPHCNames_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-CPHCNames-157">[156]</a></sup> The next nine names that were slated for use are shown below. Eight of these names were used throughout the course of the season.</p>

<ul>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_retired_Pacific_hurricane_names" title="List of retired Pacific hurricane names">List of retired Pacific hurricane names</a></div>
<p>On April 25, 2016, at the 38th session of the RA IV hurricane committee, the World Meteorological Organization officially retired the name <i>Patricia</i> due to its extreme intensity. Patricia will be replaced with <i>Pamela</i> for the 2021 Pacific hurricane season.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Season_effects">Season effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2015_Pacific_hurricane_season&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Season effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>This is a table of all the storms that have formed in the 2015 Pacific hurricane season. It includes their duration, names, landfall(s), denoted in parentheses, damages, and death totals. Deaths in parentheses are additional and indirect (an example of an indirect death would be a traffic accident), but were still related to that storm. Damage and deaths include totals while the storm was extratropical, a wave, or a low, and all the damage figures are in 2015 USD.</p>
<table align="center" border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="background:transparent;text-align:center">

<td colspan="7" nowrap="nowrap"><small><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saffir%E2%80%93Simpson_hurricane_wind_scale" title="Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale">Saffir–Simpson hurricane wind scale</a></small></td>
</tr>

<td style="background-color:#ffffcc;width:1.8em" title="Category 1: 74–95 mph (118–153 km/h)">C1</td>

<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-7"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-7">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The totals represent the sum of the squares for every (sub)tropical storm's intensity of over 33 knots (38 mph, 61 km/h), divided by 10,000. Calculations are provided at <a href="/wiki/Talk:2015_Pacific_hurricane_season/ACE_calcs" title="Talk:2015 Pacific hurricane season/ACE calcs">Talk:2015 Pacific hurricane season/ACE calcs</a>.</span></li>
